and test results are provided in the attached earthwork observation and testing report dated

Subject
Earthwork Observation and Testing Report
Ka Makana Ali i Shopping Center

Reference Report by Geolabs Inc dated
entitled Geotechnical Engineering Exploration
Ka Makana Ali i
New Phase 1 Development
Kapolei Oahu Hawaii
Grading Permit No
Dear Mr Hartline
This report summarizes our earthwork observation and testing services performed
during the grading and infrastructure installation work for the Ka Makana Ali i Shopping
Center Phase 1 project from through
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
The Ka Makana Ali i development approximately 67 acres is in the East Kapolei
area in the District of Ewa on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project site is bounded
approximately by Kapolei Parkway to the north Roosevelt Avenue to the south the
proposed Phase II North South Road Extension to the east and a drainage channel and
Kapolei Middle School to the west
Based on the information provided it is desired to develop the property into a
commercial retail center providing approximately square feet of retail and or
commercial space We understand the project will be constructed in two separate phases
The Phase 1 portion of the development will encompass about 50 acres over the northern
and central portions of the property The Phase 2 portion of the development will
encompass the remaining 17 acres of the development situated over the existing borrow
pit along the southern boundary of the property adjacent to the Phase 1 development
Page 2
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
The new buildings generally will consist of one and two story structures with the
exception of the hotel development up to six levels Some of the building areas will be
developed into building pads In addition the Phase 1 development will include open
parking lots providing over 2 500 parking spaces New driveways and underground utility
lines will also be constructed at the project site The layout of the commercial retail center
development is shown on the Site Plan Plate 1
EARTHWORK OPERATIONS
Royal Contracting Co Ltd performed the site grading operations pavement
construction and utility line installation The site grading work consisted of subgrade
preparation placement and compaction of fills and backfills pavement construction and
utility trench excavation and backfill
Following the clearing and grubbing operations the excavated subgrades or areas
designated to receive fills were scarified to a minimum depth of 12 inches
moisture conditioned to at least 2 percent above the optimum moisture content and
compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density as determined in
accordance with ASTM D1557 Modified Proctor The compaction requirement was
increased to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction for finished subgrades
subjected to vehicular traffic
The prepared subgrades were then over excavated where necessary to
approximately 24 inches below the building slabs below the cushion fill layer and
sidewalk slabs and to approximately 18 inches below the pavement structural sections to
provide the recommended non expansive select granular fill layer
During placement of the non expansive select granular fill layer the fill materials
were generally placed in near level lifts brought to above the optimum moisture content
and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density determined in
accordance with ASTM D1557 Modified Proctor The base course under the AC
pavement was generally placed in near level lifts brought to above the optimum moisture
content and compacted to a minimum of 95 percent of the maximum dry density
determined in accordance with ASTM D1557 Modified Proctor During the foundation
excavation and preparation the excavated footing bottom was generally recompacted to a
minimum of 90 percent relative compaction
New utility connections were installed to serve the new development In general a
bedding layer consisting of 6 inches of No 3B Fine gravel was provided below the piping
and manholes for uniform support Free draining granular materials consisting of
No 3B Fine gravel was also used for the trench backfill up to about 12 inches above the
pipes to provide adequate support around the pipes and to reduce the compaction effort
on the initial trench backfill The trench backfill was placed in 8 inch level loose lifts and
mechanically compacted to no less than 90 percent relative compaction Where trenches
are below pavement areas the upper 3 feet of the trench backfill below the pavement
grade was compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction
Page 3
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
During the site grading operations samples of the on site and imported materials
utilized as fill and backfill materials were obtained and transported to our office for testing
The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were established in our
laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D1557 Modified Proctor and the test
results are summarized on Plates 2 1 through 2 3
Field density tests were performed during the fill and backfill operations on an
as needed basis to confirm our field observations as variations in construction procedures
and soil conditions were noted A total of 2 934 field density tests were performed using
the nuclear probe method in accordance with ASTM D6938 Results of the compaction
tests performed are summarized on Plates 3 1 through 3 196 of this report These tests
were performed on the prepared ground surfaces and on constructed fills and backfills at
the site Test locations and elevations were estimated by pacing and interpolating from on
site survey stakes These locations and elevations should be considered accurate only to
the degree implied by the methods used Areas assessed to be unsatisfactory were
reworked until the specified minimum compaction was obtained
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the
referenced tests it is our opinion that the earthwork operations during the site grading
pavement and utility line construction for the above project observed and tested by
Geolabs in the period covered by this report were performed in general accordance with
the intent of the project plans and specifications and our geotechnical recommendations
presented in the above referenced geotechnical engineering report and
subsequent recommendations
LIMITATIONS
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site Therefore some of the earthwork were
performed without our observation However the level of earthwork observation and
testing services provided appear to be reasonable in reducing some of the geotechnical
risks to the project It should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy and
statistical repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor earthwork construction
and materials
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of
geotechnical engineering practice no warranty is expressed or implied Provision of
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance nor does it guarantee
construction of any type The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the
work for adhering to the plans and specifications and for repairing defects regardless of
when they are found
4 Page 4
CLOSURE
We appreciate the opportunity to be of continued service to you on this project If
you have questions or need additional information please contact our office
Respectfully submitted
